**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Code Review: Apache Kafka Security Defects

You are reviewing a pull request to the Apache Kafka project (`apache/kafka` tag 3.8.0). The PR modifies authentication and authorization logic in the security subsystem.

**Your task:** Find **all injected defects** in the modified code and propose fixes as unified diffs.

## Modified Files

The PR touches 4 files in the Kafka security subsystem:

1. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java`
2. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java`
3. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/CredentialCache.java`
4. `core/src/main/scala/kafka/security/authorizer/AclAuthorizer.scala`

These files handle SCRAM authentication, SASL server authentication, credential caching, and ACL-based authorization.

## What to Look For

Focus on security-critical defects including but not limited to:

- **Authentication bypass**: Missing or inverted credential validation checks
- **Authorization bypass**: Missing or inverted ACL permission checks
- **Credential validation**: Weakened iteration counts, disabled timing-attack protections
- **Token/session management**: Missing expiry checks, unsafe credential caching
- **Input validation**: Missing bounds checks, unsafe string comparisons

## Expected Output

Create `/workspace/review.json` with this structure:

```json
[
  {
    "file": "clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java",
    "line": 123,
    "severity": "critical",
    "description": "Brief description of the defect",
    "fix_patch": "--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java\n@@ -120,5 +120,5 @@\n-    old line\n+    new line\n"
  }
]
```

Each entry must include:
- `file` — Relative path from repository root
- `line` — Approximate line number where the defect occurs
- `severity` — One of: `critical`, `high`, `medium`
- `description` — What the defect is and what impact it has
- `fix_patch` — Unified diff showing the proposed fix (use `--- a/` and `+++ b/` prefix format)

**Severity levels**: Use `critical` for authentication/authorization bypasses, `high` for credential validation weaknesses, `medium` for other security issues.

**Do NOT edit source files directly.** Express all fixes as unified diffs in your review report. The evaluation system will apply your patches and verify correctness.

## Evaluation

Your review will be evaluated on:
- **Detection accuracy** (50%): Precision and recall of reported defects
- **Fix quality** (50%): Whether your proposed patches correctly resolve the defects

## Constraints

- **Time limit**: 1200 seconds
- Do NOT edit source files directly — express fixes only in `fix_patch`
- Do NOT run tests — the evaluation system handles verification

## Notes

- The workspace contains the full Kafka 3.8.0 source tree
- All defects are realistic, subtle security bugs that could plausibly appear in code review
- Some defects may require understanding interactions between multiple files
- This is a **security-focused** review — prioritize finding all authentication and authorization defects

92026-03-11T17:54:36.882993agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Let me now carefully analyze each of the 4 files for security defects. Let me look at the relevant parts:

## 1. ScramSaslServer.java

Looking at `verifyClientProof` (lines 225-235):
```java
private void verifyClientProof(ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage) throws SaslException {
    try {
        byte[] expectedStoredKey = scramCredential.storedKey();
        byte[] clientSignature = formatter.clientSignature(expectedStoredKey, clientFirstMessage, serverFirstMessage, clientFinalMessage);
        byte[] computedStoredKey = formatter.storedKey(clientSignature, clientFinalMessage.proof());
        if (!MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey))
            throw new SaslException("Invalid client credentials");
    } catch (InvalidKeyException e) {
        throw new SaslException("Sasl client verification failed", e);
    }
}
```

This looks correct. The SCRAM verification:
1. Gets expected stored key from credential
2. Computes client signature using stored key
3. Computes stored key from client signature and proof
4. Compares computed stored key with expected stored key using timing-safe comparison `MessageDigest.isEqual`

This looks correct to me. Let me check the original Apache Kafka code to compare.

Looking at line 135:
```java
if (scramCredential.iterations() < mechanism.minIterations())
    throw new SaslException("Iterations ..." ...);
```
This is correct - rejecting credentials with too few iterations.

Looking at line 132:
```java
if (!authorizationIdFromClient.isEmpty() && !authorizationIdFromClient.equals(username))
    throw new SaslAuthenticationException("Authentication failed: Client requested an authorization id that is different from username");
```
This is correct - rejecting if authorizationId != username.

222026-03-11T18:04:27.215623agentmessage-
I am thinking...: OK, now I can see the ScramFormatter fully. Let me verify the `verifyClientProof` implementation in `ScramSaslServer.java`:

```java
private void verifyClientProof(ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage) throws SaslException {
    try {
        byte[] expectedStoredKey = scramCredential.storedKey();
        byte[] clientSignature = formatter.clientSignature(expectedStoredKey, clientFirstMessage, serverFirstMessage, clientFinalMessage);
        byte[] computedStoredKey = formatter.storedKey(clientSignature, clientFinalMessage.proof());
        if (!MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey))
            throw new SaslException("Invalid client credentials");
    } catch (InvalidKeyException e) {
        throw new SaslException("Sasl client verification failed", e);
    }
}
```

And the `ScramFormatter.storedKey(byte[] clientSignature, byte[] clientProof)`:
```java
public byte[] storedKey(byte[] clientSignature, byte[] clientProof) {
    return hash(xor(clientSignature, clientProof));
}
```

So `computedStoredKey = hash(xor(clientSignature, clientProof)) = hash(xor(HMAC(storedKey, authMsg), clientProof))`

From the SCRAM protocol:
- `ClientProof = ClientKey XOR ClientSignature`
- `ClientSignature = HMAC(StoredKey, AuthMessage)` 
- `StoredKey = H(ClientKey)`

So:
- `ClientKey = ClientProof XOR ClientSignature = ClientProof XOR HMAC(StoredKey, AuthMessage)`
- To verify: `H(ClientKey) = StoredKey`

In the code:
- `clientSignature = HMAC(expectedStoredKey, authMessage)` ✓
- `computedStoredKey = hash(xor(clientSignature, proof))` = `H(xor(HMAC(StoredKey, AuthMessage), ClientProof))`

But `xor(HMAC(StoredKey, AuthMessage), ClientProof) = xor(ClientSignature, ClientProof)` = `ClientKey` (since ClientProof = ClientKey XOR ClientSignature, so Clien
... (truncated)

The session expiry is checked by the Kafka network layer. When `serverSessionExpirationTimeNanos()` returns a non-null value, the network layer will force reauthentication when the time expires. If the server reports the wrong expiry, sessions could last longer than intended.

Looking at `calcCompletionTimesAndReturnSessionLifetimeMs`:

This computes `authenticationEndNanos + retvalSessionLifetimeMs * nanosPerMs`. If `retvalSessionLifetimeMs = 0` (session already expired or no expiry set), then `sessionExpirationTimeNanos = authenticationEndNanos`, meaning the session expires immediately. The network layer would immediate

## Security Review Summary

### Files Reviewed
1. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java` — No defects found. The SCRAM proof verification correctly uses `MessageDigest.isEqual` (timing-safe), the iteration count check uses the correct `<` operator, and authorization ID validation is correct.

Re-authentication principal check (`ensurePrincipalUnchanged`) is correct, session lifetime computation uses `Math.min` correctly, and the `connectedClientSupportsReauthentication` flag logic is correct.
3. `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/CredentialCache.java` — No defects found. Standard concurrent hash map wrapper with correct `putIfAbsent`/return-value logic.
4. `core/src/main/scala/kafka/security/authorizer/AclAuthorizer.scala` — **1 critical defect found.**

### Defect Found

**`AclAuthorizer.scala` lines 377–380 — Authorization Bypass (critical)**

The `shouldAllowEveryoneIfNoAclIsFound` check in `authorizeByResourceType` is placed immediately after the wildcard-deny check (`denyAll`) but **before** prefixed deny ACLs (`denyPrefixes`) are even fetched. When `allow.everyone.if.no.acl.found=true`, this causes the method to return `ALLOWED` without ever evaluating prefixed DENY ACLs. An administrator who configures a prefixed deny rule (e.g., denying access to all topics starting with `"internal_"`) would have that rule completely bypassed for any principal when the configuration flag is enabled.

**Fix:** Remove the premature `shouldAllowEveryoneIfNoAclIsFound` block at lines 377–380 and move the check inside

@SuppressWarnings(\\\\\\\"fallthrough\\\\\\\")\\\\n247:     @Override\\\\n248:     public void authenticate() throws IOException {\\\\n249:         if (saslState != SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE)         }\\\\n545:                     LOG.debug(\\\\\\\"Received client packet of length {} starting with bytes 0x{}, process as GSSAPI packet\\\\\\\", requestBytes.length, tokenBuilder);\\\\n546:                 }\\\\n547:                 if (enabledMechanisms.contains(SaslConfigs.GSSAPI_MECHANISM)) {\\\\n548:                     LOG.debug(\\\\\\\"First client packet is not a SASL mechanism \\\\n563:     private String handleHandshakeRequest(RequestContext context, SaslHandshakeRequest handshakeRequest) throws IOException, UnsupportedSaslMechanismException {\\\\n564:         String clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism();\\\\n565:         short version = context.header.apiVersion();\\\\n566:         if (version \\\\u003e= 1)\\\\n567: void handleApiVersionsRequest(RequestContext context, ApiVersionsRequest apiVersionsRequest) throws IOException {\\\\n587:         if (saslState != SaslState.HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST)\\\\n588:             throw new IllegalStateException(\\\\\\\"Unexpected ApiVersions request received during SASL authentication state \\\\\\\" + saslState);\\\\n589: \\\\n590:         if   "message": "## Task Complete\n\nI've completed the security code review of the four modified Kafka files and produced `/workspace/review.json` with my findings.\n\n### Finding\n\n**1 critical defect \u2014 `AclAuthorizer.scala` line 377**\n\n**What:** In `authorizeByResourceType`, the `shouldAllowEveryoneIfNoAclIsFound` guard block (lines 377\u2013380) is placed immediately after the wildcard-deny check (`denyAll`) but *before* prefixed deny ACLs are fetched. When `allow.everyone.if.no.acl.found=true`, the method returns `ALLOWED` without ever evaluating `DENY` ACLs of `PatternType.PREFIXED`.\n\n**Impact:** A principal with an explicit prefixed-deny rule (e.g., DENY WRITE on all topics with prefix `\"internal_\"`) can bypass that rule entirely and gain access whenever the open-default config is enabled. This is an authorization bypass.\n\n**Fix:** Remove the four lines at 377\u2013380 and move the `shouldAllowEveryoneIfNoAclIsFound` fallback into the `denyLiterals.isEmpty && denyPrefixes.isEmpty` block as an `else if` branch \u2014 so it only fires when there are genuinely no ACLs at all, which is the correct semantic (\"when no ACLs are found for a resource, allow everyone\"). This matches the analogous `isEmptyAclAndAuthorized` logic used in `authorizeAction`.\n\nThe other three files (`ScramSaslServer.java`, `SaslServerAuthenticator.java`, `CredentialCache.java`) were examined thoroughly and no injected defects were found in them."
